         </b>

         </a>
         <b>
          ·
         </b>
         <a class="external text" href="http://tripgang.com/kml2gpx/http%3A%2F%2Ftools.wmflabs.org%2Fkmlexport%3Farticle%3DList_of_solar_eclipses_in_the_10th_century?gpx=1" rel="nofollow">
          GPX
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       This is a
       <b>
        list of solar eclipses in the 10th century
       </b>
       . During the period 901 to 1000 there were 227
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse" title="Solar eclipse">
        solar eclipses
       </a>
       of which 76 were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partial_solar_eclipse" title="Partial solar eclipse">
        Partial
       </a>
       , 84 were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annular_solar_eclipse" title="Annular solar eclipse">
        annular
       </a>
       (one
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse#Terminology" title="Solar eclipse">
        non-central
       </a>
       ), 66 were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Total_solar_eclipse" title="Total solar eclipse">
        total
       </a>
       (one non-central), and 1 was
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hybrid_solar_eclipse" title="Hybrid solar eclipse">
        hybrid
       </a>
       . The greatest number of eclipses in one year was four, in 911, 922, 940, 958, and 991.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_catalog_list_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nasa_catalog_list-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dates are given using the
       <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">
        Julian calendar
       </a>
       .
      </p>
